fmt::Display for ImplPolarity {\n   222→    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n   223→        match self {\n   224→            Self::Positive => f.write_str(\"positive\"),\n   225→            Self::Negative => f.write_str(\"negative\"),\n   226→            Self::Reservation => f.write_str(\"reservation\"),\n   227→        }\n   228→    }\n   229→}\n   230→\n   231→impl ImplPolarity {\n   232→    /// The polarity marker in front of the impl trait ref if applicable.\n   233→    pub fn as_str(self) -> &'static str {\n   234→        match self {\n   235→            Self::Positive => \"\",\n   236→            Self::Negative => \"!\",\n   237→            Self::Reservation => \"\",\n   238→        }\n   239→    }\n   240→}\n   241→\n   242→/// Polarity for a trait predicate. May either be negative or positive.\n   243→/// Distinguished from [`ImplPolarity`] since we never compute goals with\n   244→/// \"reservation\" level.\n   245→#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n   246→#[cfg_attr(\n   247→    feature = \"nightly\",\n   248→    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n   249→)]\n   250→pub enum PredicatePolarity {\n   251→    /// `Type: Trait`\n   252→    Positive,\n   253→    /// `Type: !Trait`\n   254→    Negative,\n   255→}\n   256→\n   257→impl PredicatePolarity {\n   258→    /// Flips polarity by turning `Positive` into `Negative` and `Negative` into `Positive`.\n   259→    pub fn flip(&self) -> PredicatePolarity {\n   260→        match self {\n   261→            PredicatePolarity::Positive => PredicatePolarity::Negative,\n   262→            PredicatePolarity::Negative => PredicatePolarity::Positive,\n   263→        }\n   264→    }\n   265→}\n   266→\n   267→impl fmt::Display for PredicatePolarity {\n   268→    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n   269→        match self {\n   270→            Self::Positive => f.write_str(\"positive\"),\n   271→            Self::Negative => f.write_str(\"negative\"),\n   272→        }\n   273→    }\n   274→}\n   275→\n   276→#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n   277→#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n   278→#[cfg_attr(\n   279→    feature = \"nightly\",\n   280→    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n   281→)]\n   282→pub enum ExistentialPredicate<I: Interner> {\n   283→    /// E.g., `Iterator`.\n   284→    Trait(ExistentialTraitRef<I>),\n   285→    /// E.g., `Iterator::Item = T`.\n   286→    Projection(ExistentialProjection<I>),\n   287→    /// E.g., `Send`.\n   288→    AutoTrait(I::TraitId),\n   289→}\n   290→\n   291→impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialPredicate<I> {}\n   292→\n   293→impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialPredicate<I>> {\n   294→    /// Given an existential predicate like `?Self: PartialEq<u32>` (e.g., derived from `dyn PartialEq<u32>`),\n   295→    /// and a concrete type `self_ty`, returns a full predicate where the existentially quantified variable `?Self`\n   296→    /// has been replaced with `self_ty` (e.g., `self_ty: PartialEq<u32>`, in our example).\n   297→    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> I::Clause {\n   298→        match self.skip_binder() {\n   299→            ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => self.rebind(tr).with_self_ty(cx, self_ty).upcast(cx),\n   300→            ExistentialPredicate::Projection(p) => {\n   301→                self.rebind(p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty)).upcast(cx)\n   302→            }\n   303→            ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => {\n   304→                let generics = cx.generics_of(did.into());\n   305→                let trait_ref = if generics.count() == 1 {\n   306→                    ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\n   307→                } else {\n   308→                    // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\n   309→                    // new error args for the missing generics.\n   310→                    let err_args =\n   311→                        GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\n   312→                    ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\n   313→                };\n   314→                self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\n   315→            }\n   316→        }\n   317→    }\n   318→}\n   319→\n   320→/// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\n   321→/// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\n   322→/// ```ignore (illustrative)\n   323→/// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\n   324→/// ```\n   325→/// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\n   326→/// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\n   327→#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n   328→#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n   329→#[cfg_attr(\n   330→    feature = \"nightly\",\n   331→    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n   332→)]\n   333→pub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\n   334→    pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n   335→    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n   336→    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\n   337→    /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\n   338→    _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n   339→}\n   340→\n   341→impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\n   342→\n   343→impl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n   344→    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n   345→        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n   346→        Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n   347→    }\n   348→\n   349→    pub fn new(\n   350→        interner: I,\n   351→        trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n   352→        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n   353→    ) -> Self {\n   354→        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n   355→        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n   356→    }\n   357→\n   358→    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n   359→        // Assert there is a Self.\n   360→        trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\n   361→\n   362→        ExistentialTraitRef {\n   363→            def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\n   364→            args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n   365→            _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n   366→        }\n   367→    }\n   368→\n   369→    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n   370→    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n   371→    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n   372→    /// or some placeholder type.\n   373→    pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\n   374→        // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\n   375→        // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n   376→\n   377→        TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\n   378→    }\n   379→}\n   380→\n   381→impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\n   382→    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n   383→        self.skip_binder().def_id\n   384→    }\n   385→\n   386→    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n   387→    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n   388→    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n   389→    /// or some placeholder type.\n   390→    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n   391→        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n   392→    }\n   393→}\n   394→\n   395→/// A `ProjectionPredicate` for an `ExistentialTraitRef`.\n   396→#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n   397→#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n   398→#[cfg_attr(\n   399→    feature = \"nightly\",\n   400→    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n   401→)]\n   402→pub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\n   403→    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n   404→    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n   405→    pub term: I::Term,\n   406→\n   407→    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\n   408→    /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\n   409→    use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n   410→}\n   411→\n   412→impl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\n   413→\n   414→impl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n   415→    pub fn new_from_args(\n   416→        interner: I,\n   417→        def_id: I::DefId,\n   418→        args: I::GenericArgs,\n   419→        term: I::Term,\n   420→    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n   421→        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n   422→        Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\n   423→    }\n   424→\n   425→    pub fn new(\n   426→        interner: I,\n   427→        def_id: I::DefId,\n   428→        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n   429→        term: I::Term,\n   430→    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n   431→        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n   432→        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\n   433→    }\n   434→\n   435→    /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\n   436→    /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\n   437→    /// then this function would return an `exists T. T: Iterator` existential trait\n   438→    /// reference.\n   439→    pub fn trait_ref(&self, interner: I) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n   440→        let def_id = interner.parent(self.def_id);\n   441→        let args_count = interner.generics_of(def_id).count() - 1;\n   442→        let args = interner.mk_args(&self.args.as_slice()[..args_count]);\n   443→        ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args(interner, def_id.try_into().unwrap(), args)\n   444→    }\n   445→\n   446→    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n   447→        // otherwise the escaping regions would be captured by the binders\n   448→        debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n   449→\n   450→        ProjectionPredicate {\n   451→            projection_term: AliasTerm::new(\n   452→                interner,\n   453→                self.def_id,\n   454→                [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\n   455→            ),\n   456→            term: self.term,\n   457→        }\n   458→    }\n   459→\n   460→    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, projection_predicate: ProjectionPredicate<I>) -> Self {\n   461→        // Assert there is a Self.\n   462→        projection_predicate.projection_term.args.type_at(0);\n   463→\n   464→        Self {\n   465→            def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\n   466→            args: interner.mk_args(&projection_predicate.projection_term.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n   467→            term: projection_predicate.term,\n   468→            use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n   469→        }\n   470→    }\n   471→}\n   472→\n   473→impl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\n   474→    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n   475→        self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n   476→    }\n   477→\n   478→    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n   479→        self.skip_binder().def_id\n   480→    }\n   481→}\n   482→\n   483→#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n   484→#[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\n   485→pub enum AliasTermKind {\n   486→    /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n   487→    /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n   488→    ProjectionTy,\n   489→    /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n   490→    InherentTy,\n   491→    /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n   492→    /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n   493→    OpaqueTy,\n   494→    /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n   495→    /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n   496→    /// Can always be normalized away.\n   497→    FreeTy,\n   498→\n   499→    /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\n   500→    UnevaluatedConst,\n   501→    /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\n   502→    ProjectionConst,\n   503→    /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\n   504→    FreeConst,\n   505→    /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\n   506→    InherentConst,\n   507→}\n   508→\n   509→impl AliasTermKind {\n   510→    pub fn descr(self) -> &'static str {\n   511→        match self {\n   512→            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => \"associated type\",\n   513→            AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n   514→            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n   515→            AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n   516→            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n   517→            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n   518→            AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n   519→            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n   520→        }\n   521→    }\n   522→\n   523→    pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n   524→        match self {\n   525→            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n   526→            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n   527→            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n   528→            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => true,\n   529→\n   530→            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n   531→            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n   532→            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n   533→            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n   534→        }\n   535→    }\n   536→}\n   537→\n   538→impl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n   539→    fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n   540→        match value {\n   541→            ty::Projection => AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy,\n   542→            ty::Opaque => AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy,\n   543→            ty::Free => AliasTermKind::FreeTy,\n   544→            ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n   545→        }\n   546→    }\n   547→}\n   548→\n   549→/// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n   550→///\n   551→/// * For a projection, this would be `<Ty as Trait<...>>::N<...>`.\n   552→/// * For an inherent projection, this would be `Ty::N<...>`.\n   553→/// * For an opaque type, there is no explicit syntax.\n   554→#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n   555→#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n   556→#[cfg_attr(\n   557→    feature = \"nightly\",\n   558→    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n   559→)]\n   560→pub struct AliasTerm<I: Interner> {\n   561→    /// The parameters of the associated or opaque item.\n   562→    ///\n   563→    /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n   564→    /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n   565→    ///\n   566→    /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\n   567→    /// if there are any.\n   568→    ///\n   569→    /// For RPIT the generic parameters are for the generics of the function,\n   570→    /// while for TAIT it is used for the generic parameters of the alias.\n   571→    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n   572→\n   573→    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` or `ImplItem` for the associated type `N` depending on whether\n   574→    /// this is a projection or an inherent projection or the `DefId` of the `OpaqueType` item if\n   575→    /// this is an opaque.\n   576→    ///\n   577→    /// During codegen, `interner.type_of(def_id)` can be used to get the type of the\n   578→    /// underlying type if the type is an opaque.\n   579→    ///\n   580→    /// Note that if this is an associated type, this is not the `DefId` of the\n   581→    /// `TraitRef` containing this associated type, which is in `interner.associated_item(def_id).container`,\n   582→    /// aka. `interner.parent(def_id)`.\n   583→    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n   584→\n   585→    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `AliasTerm` without using [`AliasTerm::new_from_args`].\n   586→    #[derive_where(skip(Debug))]\n   587→    _use_alias_term_new_instead: (),\n   588→}\n   589→\n   590→impl<I: Interner> Eq for AliasTerm<I> {}\n   591→\n   592→impl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n   593→    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, def_id: I::DefId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n   594→        interner.debug_assert_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n   595→        AliasTerm { def_id, args, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n   596→    }\n   597→\n   598→    pub fn new(\n   599→        interner: I,\n   600→        def_id: I::DefId,\n   601→        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n   602→    ) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n   603→        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n   604→        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args)\n   605→    }\n   606→\n   607→    pub fn expect_ty(self, interner: I) -> ty::AliasTy<I> {\n   608→        match self.kind(interner) {\n   609→            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n   610→            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n   611→            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n   612→            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => {}\n   613→            AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n   614→            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n   615→            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n   616→            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => {\n   617→                panic!(\"Cannot turn `UnevaluatedConst` into `AliasTy`\")\n   618→            }\n   619→        }\n   620→        ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () }\n   621→    }\n   622→\n   623→    pub fn kind(self, interner: I) -> AliasTermKind {\n   624→        interner.alias_term_kind(self)\n   625→    }\n   626→\n   627→    pub fn to_term(self, interner: I) -> I::Term {\n   628→        match self.kind(interner) {\n   629→            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => Ty::new_alias(\n   630→                interner,\n   631→                ty::AliasTyKind::Projection,\n   632→                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n   633→            )\n   634→            .into(),\n   635→            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => Ty::new_alias(\n   636→                interner,\n   637→                ty::AliasTyKind::Inherent,\n   638→                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n   639→            )\n   640→            .into(),\n   641→            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => Ty::new_alias(\n   642→                interner,\n   643→                ty::AliasTyKind::Opaque,\n   644→                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n   645→            )\n   646→            .into(),\n   647→            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => Ty::new_alias(\n   648→                interner,\n   649→                ty::AliasTyKind::Free,\n   650→                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n   651→            )\n   652→            .into(),\n   653→            AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n   654→            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n   655→            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n   656→            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => I::Const::new_unevaluated(\n   657→                interner,\n   658→                ty::UnevaluatedConst::new(self.def_id.try_into().unwrap(), self.args),\n   659→            )\n   660→            .into(),\n   661→        }\n   662→    }\n   663→}\n   664→\n   665→/// The following methods work only with (trait) associated term projections.\n   666→impl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n   667→    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n   668→        self.args.type_at(0)\n   669→    }\n   670→\n   671→    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n   672→        AliasTerm::new(\n   673→            interner,\n   674→            self.def_id,\n   675→            [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)),\n   676→        )\n   677→    }\n   678→\n   679→    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n   680→        assert!(\n   681→            matches!(\n   682→                self.kind(interner),\n   683→                AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n   684→            ),\n   685→            \"expected a projection\"\n   686→        );\n   687→        interner.parent(self.def_id).try_into().unwrap()\n   688→    }\n   689→\n   690→    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference and own args from this projection.\n   691→    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n   692→    /// then this function would return a `T: StreamingIterator` trait reference and\n   693→    /// `['a]` as the own args.\n   694→    pub fn trait_ref_and_own_args(self, interner: I) -> (TraitRef<I>, I::GenericArgsSlice) {\n   695→        interner.trait_ref_and_own_args_for_alias(self.def_id, self.args)\n   696→    }\n   697→\n   698→    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference from this projection.\n   699→    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as Iterator>::Item`,\n   700→    /// then this function would return a `T: Iterator` trait reference.\n   701→    ///\n   702→    /// WARNING: This will drop the args for generic associated types\n   703→    /// consider calling [Self::trait_ref_and_own_args] to get those\n   704→    /// as well.\n   705→    pub fn trait_ref(self, interner: I) -> TraitRef<I> {\n   706→        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).0\n   707→    }\n   708→\n   709→    /// Extract the own args from this projection.\n   710→    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n   711→    /// then this function would return the slice `['a]` as the own args.\n   712→    pub fn own_args(self, interner: I) -> I::GenericArgsSlice {\n   713→        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).1\n   714→    }\n   715→}\n   716→\n   717→/// The following methods work only with inherent associated term projections.\n   718→impl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n   719→    /// Transform the generic parameters to have the given `impl` args as the base and the GAT args on top of that.\n   720→    ///\n   721→    /// Does the following transformation:\n   722→    ///\n   723→    /// ```text\n   724→    /// [Self, ty::TraitRef::new(cx, did, [self_ty])\n                } else {\n                    // If this is an ill-formed auto trait, then synthesize\n                    // new error args for the missing generics.\n                    let err_args =\n                        GenericArgs::extend_with_error(cx, did.into(), &[self_ty.into()]);\n                    ty::TraitRef::new_from_args(cx, did, err_args)\n                };\n                self.rebind(trait_ref).upcast(cx)\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// An existential reference to a trait, where `Self` is erased.\n/// For example, the trait object `Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>` is:\n/// ```ignore (illustrative)\n/// exists T. T: Trait<'a, 'b, X, Y>\n/// ```\n/// The generic parameters don't include the erased `Self`, only trait\n/// type and lifetime parameters (`[X, Y]` and `['a, 'b]` above).\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialTraitRef<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::TraitId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialTraitRef` without\n    /// calling [`ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args`].\n    _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialTraitRef<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, trait_def_id: I::TraitId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> Self {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(trait_def_id.into(), args);\n        Self { def_id: trait_def_id, args, _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        trait_def_id: I::TraitId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, trait_def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, trait_ref: TraitRef<I>) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        trait_ref.args.type_at(0);\n\n        ExistentialTraitRef {\n            def_id: trait_ref.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&trait_ref.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            _use_existential_trait_ref_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping vars would be captured by the binder\n        // debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        TraitRef::new(interner, self.def_id, [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter()))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialTraitRef<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(&self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n\n    /// Object types don't have a self type specified. Therefore, when\n    /// we convert the principal trait-ref into a normal trait-ref,\n    /// you must give *some* self type. A common choice is `mk_err()`\n    /// or some placeholder type.\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, TraitRef<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `ProjectionPredicate` for an `ExistentialTraitRef`.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ExistentialProjection<I: Interner> {\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `ExistentialProjection`\n    /// without using [`ExistentialProjection::new_from_args`].\n    use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ExistentialProjection<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: I::GenericArgs,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_existential_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        Self { def_id, args, term, use_existential_projection_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n        term: I::Term,\n    ) -> ExistentialProjection<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args, term)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying existential trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `exists T. <T as Iterator>::Item == X`,\n    /// then this function would return an `exists T. T: Iterator` existential trait\n    /// reference.\n    pub fn trait_ref(&self, interner: I) -> ExistentialTraitRef<I> {\n        let def_id = interner.parent(self.def_id);\n        let args_count = interner.generics_of(def_id).count() - 1;\n        let args = interner.mk_args(&self.args.as_slice()[..args_count]);\n        ExistentialTraitRef::new_from_args(interner, def_id.try_into().unwrap(), args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        // otherwise the escaping regions would be captured by the binders\n        debug_assert!(!self_ty.has_escaping_bound_vars());\n\n        ProjectionPredicate {\n            projection_term: AliasTerm::new(\n                interner,\n                self.def_id,\n                [self_ty.into()].iter().chain(self.args.iter()),\n            ),\n            term: self.term,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn erase_self_ty(interner: I, projection_predicate: ProjectionPredicate<I>) -> Self {\n        // Assert there is a Self.\n        projection_predicate.projection_term.args.type_at(0);\n\n        Self {\n            def_id: projection_predicate.projection_term.def_id,\n            args: interner.mk_args(&projection_predicate.projection_term.args.as_slice()[1..]),\n            term: projection_predicate.term,\n            use_existential_projection_new_instead: (),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ExistentialProjection<I>> {\n    pub fn with_self_ty(&self, cx: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n        self.map_bound(|p| p.with_self_ty(cx, self_ty))\n    }\n\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.skip_binder().def_id\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, PartialOrd, Ord, Hash, Debug)]\n#[cfg_attr(feature = \"nightly\", derive(Encodable, Decodable, HashStable_NoContext))]\npub enum AliasTermKind {\n    /// A projection `<Type as Trait>::AssocType`.\n    /// Can get normalized away if monomorphic enough.\n    ProjectionTy,\n    /// An associated type in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentTy,\n    /// An opaque type (usually from `impl Trait` in type aliases or function return types)\n    /// Can only be normalized away in PostAnalysis mode or its defining scope.\n    OpaqueTy,\n    /// A free type alias that actually checks its trait bounds.\n    /// Currently only used if the type alias references opaque types.\n    /// Can always be normalized away.\n    FreeTy,\n\n    /// An unevaluated anonymous constants.\n    UnevaluatedConst,\n    /// An unevaluated const coming from an associated const.\n    ProjectionConst,\n    /// A top level const item not part of a trait or impl.\n    FreeConst,\n    /// An associated const in an inherent `impl`\n    InherentConst,\n}\n\nimpl AliasTermKind {\n    pub fn descr(self) -> &'static str {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => \"associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => \"associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => \"inherent associated type\",\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst => \"inherent associated const\",\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => \"opaque type\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => \"type alias\",\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst => \"unevaluated constant\",\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn is_type(self) -> bool {\n        match self {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => true,\n\n            AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst => false,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl From<ty::AliasTyKind> for AliasTermKind {\n    fn from(value: ty::AliasTyKind) -> Self {\n        match value {\n            ty::Projection => AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy,\n            ty::Opaque => AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy,\n            ty::Free => AliasTermKind::FreeTy,\n            ty::Inherent => AliasTermKind::InherentTy,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Represents the unprojected term of a projection goal.\n///\n/// * For a projection, this would be `<Ty as Trait<...>>::N<...>`.\n/// * For an inherent projection, this would be `Ty::N<...>`.\n/// * For an opaque type, there is no explicit syntax.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct AliasTerm<I: Interner> {\n    /// The parameters of the associated or opaque item.\n    ///\n    /// For a projection, these are the generic parameters for the trait and the\n    /// GAT parameters, if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For an inherent projection, they consist of the self type and the GAT parameters,\n    /// if there are any.\n    ///\n    /// For RPIT the generic parameters are for the generics of the function,\n    /// while for TAIT it is used for the generic parameters of the alias.\n    pub args: I::GenericArgs,\n\n    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` or `ImplItem` for the associated type `N` depending on whether\n    /// this is a projection or an inherent projection or the `DefId` of the `OpaqueType` item if\n    /// this is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// During codegen, `interner.type_of(def_id)` can be used to get the type of the\n    /// underlying type if the type is an opaque.\n    ///\n    /// Note that if this is an associated type, this is not the `DefId` of the\n    /// `TraitRef` containing this associated type, which is in `interner.associated_item(def_id).container`,\n    /// aka. `interner.parent(def_id)`.\n    pub def_id: I::DefId,\n\n    /// This field exists to prevent the creation of `AliasTerm` without using [`AliasTerm::new_from_args`].\n    #[derive_where(skip(Debug))]\n    _use_alias_term_new_instead: (),\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for AliasTerm<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn new_from_args(interner: I, def_id: I::DefId, args: I::GenericArgs) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        interner.debug_assert_args_compatible(def_id, args);\n        AliasTerm { def_id, args, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn new(\n        interner: I,\n        def_id: I::DefId,\n        args: impl IntoIterator<Item: Into<I::GenericArg>>,\n    ) -> AliasTerm<I> {\n        let args = interner.mk_args_from_iter(args.into_iter().map(Into::into));\n        Self::new_from_args(interner, def_id, args)\n    }\n\n    pub fn expect_ty(self, interner: I) -> ty::AliasTy<I> {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentTy\n            | AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeTy => {}\n            AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => {\n                panic!(\"Cannot turn `UnevaluatedConst` into `AliasTy`\")\n            }\n        }\n        ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () }\n    }\n\n    pub fn kind(self, interner: I) -> AliasTermKind {\n        interner.alias_term_kind(self)\n    }\n\n    pub fn to_term(self, interner: I) -> I::Term {\n        match self.kind(interner) {\n            AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Projection,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Inherent,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::OpaqueTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Opaque,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeTy => Ty::new_alias(\n                interner,\n                ty::AliasTyKind::Free,\n                ty::AliasTy { def_id: self.def_id, args: self.args, _use_alias_ty_new_instead: () },\n            )\n            .into(),\n            AliasTermKind::FreeConst\n            | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n            | AliasTermKind::UnevaluatedConst\n            | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst => I::Const::new_unevaluated(\n                interner,\n                ty::UnevaluatedConst::new(self.def_id.try_into().unwrap(), self.args),\n            )\n            .into(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// The following methods work only with (trait) associated term projections.\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.args.type_at(0)\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm::new(\n            interner,\n            self.def_id,\n            [self_ty.into()].into_iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)),\n        )\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        assert!(\n            matches!(\n                self.kind(interner),\n                AliasTermKind::ProjectionTy | AliasTermKind::ProjectionConst\n            ),\n            \"expected a projection\"\n        );\n        interner.parent(self.def_id).try_into().unwrap()\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference and own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: StreamingIterator` trait reference and\n    /// `['a]` as the own args.\n    pub fn trait_ref_and_own_args(self, interner: I) -> (TraitRef<I>, I::GenericArgsSlice) {\n        interner.trait_ref_and_own_args_for_alias(self.def_id, self.args)\n    }\n\n    /// Extracts the underlying trait reference from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as Iterator>::Item`,\n    /// then this function would return a `T: Iterator` trait reference.\n    ///\n    /// WARNING: This will drop the args for generic associated types\n    /// consider calling [Self::trait_ref_and_own_args] to get those\n    /// as well.\n    pub fn trait_ref(self, interner: I) -> TraitRef<I> {\n        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).0\n    }\n\n    /// Extract the own args from this projection.\n    /// For example, if this is a projection of `<T as StreamingIterator>::Item<'a>`,\n    /// then this function would return the slice `['a]` as the own args.\n    pub fn own_args(self, interner: I) -> I::GenericArgsSlice {\n        self.trait_ref_and_own_args(interner).1\n    }\n}\n\n/// The following methods work only with inherent associated term projections.\nimpl<I: Interner> AliasTerm<I> {\n    /// Transform the generic parameters to have the given `impl` args as the base and the GAT args on top of that.\n    ///\n    /// Does the following transformation:\n    ///\n    /// ```text\n    /// [Self, P_0...P_m] -> [I_0...I_n, P_0...P_m]\n    ///\n    ///     I_i impl args\n    ///     P_j GAT args\n    /// ```\n    pub fn rebase_inherent_args_onto_impl(\n        self,\n        impl_args: I::GenericArgs,\n        interner: I,\n    ) -> I::GenericArgs {\n        debug_assert!(matches!(\n            self.kind(interner),\n            AliasTermKind::InherentTy | AliasTermKind::InherentConst\n        ));\n        interner.mk_args_from_iter(impl_args.iter().chain(self.args.iter().skip(1)))\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> From<ty::AliasTy<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\n    fn from(ty: ty::AliasTy<I>) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm { args: ty.args, def_id: ty.def_id, _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> From<ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>> for AliasTerm<I> {\n    fn from(ct: ty::UnevaluatedConst<I>) -> Self {\n        AliasTerm { args: ct.args, def_id: ct.def.into(), _use_alias_term_new_instead: () }\n    }\n}\n\n/// This kind of predicate has no *direct* correspondent in the\n/// syntax, but it roughly corresponds to the syntactic forms:\n///\n/// 1. `T: TraitRef<..., Item = Type>`\n/// 2. `<T as TraitRef<...>>::Item == Type` (NYI)\n///\n/// In particular, form #1 is \"desugared\" to the combination of a\n/// normal trait predicate (`T: TraitRef<...>`) and one of these\n/// predicates. Form #2 is a broader form in that it also permits\n/// equality between arbitrary types. Processing an instance of\n/// Form #2 eventually yields one of these `ProjectionPredicate`\n/// instances to normalize the LHS.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct ProjectionPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub projection_term: AliasTerm<I>,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for ProjectionPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.projection_term.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n        Self {\n            projection_term: self.projection_term.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty),\n            ..self\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.projection_term.trait_def_id(interner)\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.projection_term.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, ProjectionPredicate<I>> {\n    /// Returns the `DefId` of the trait of the associated item being projected.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn trait_def_id(&self, cx: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.skip_binder().projection_term.trait_def_id(cx)\n    }\n\n    pub fn term(&self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Term> {\n        self.map_bound(|predicate| predicate.term)\n    }\n\n    /// The `DefId` of the `TraitItem` for the associated type.\n    ///\n    /// Note that this is not the `DefId` of the `TraitRef` containing this\n    /// associated type, which is in `tcx.associated_item(projection_def_id()).container`.\n    pub fn item_def_id(&self) -> I::DefId {\n        // Ok to skip binder since trait `DefId` does not care about regions.\n        self.skip_binder().projection_term.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> fmt::Debug for ProjectionPredicate<I> {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        write!(f, \"ProjectionPredicate({:?}, {:?})\", self.projection_term, self.term)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Used by the new solver to normalize an alias. This always expects the `term` to\n/// be an unconstrained inference variable which is used as the output.\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Decodable_NoContext, Encodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct NormalizesTo<I: Interner> {\n    pub alias: AliasTerm<I>,\n    pub term: I::Term,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for NormalizesTo<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> NormalizesTo<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.alias.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> NormalizesTo<I> {\n        Self { alias: self.alias.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty), ..self }\n    }\n\n    pub fn trait_def_id(self, interner: I) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.alias.trait_def_id(interner)\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::DefId {\n        self.alias.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> fmt::Debug for NormalizesTo<I> {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        write!(f, \"NormalizesTo({:?}, {:?})\", self.alias, self.term)\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive_where(Clone, Copy, Hash, PartialEq, Debug; I: Interner)]\n#[derive(TypeVisitable_Generic, TypeFoldable_Generic, Lift_Generic)]\n#[cfg_attr(\n    feature = \"nightly\",\n    derive(Encodable_NoContext, Decodable_NoContext, HashStable_NoContext)\n)]\npub struct HostEffectPredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub trait_ref: ty::TraitRef<I>,\n    pub constness: BoundConstness,\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> Eq for HostEffectPredicate<I> {}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> HostEffectPredicate<I> {\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> I::Ty {\n        self.trait_ref.self_ty()\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_replaced_self_ty(self, interner: I, self_ty: I::Ty) -> Self {\n        Self { trait_ref: self.trait_ref.with_replaced_self_ty(interner, self_ty), ..self }\n    }\n\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::TraitId {\n        self.trait_ref.def_id\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<I: Interner> ty::Binder<I, HostEffectPredicate<I>> {\n    pub fn def_id(self) -> I::TraitId {\n        // Ok to skip binder since trait `DefId` does not care about regions.\n        self.skip_binder().def_id()\n    }\n\n    pub fn self_ty(self) -> ty::Binder<I, I::Ty> {\n        self.map_bound(|trait_ref| trait_ref.self_ty())\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn constness(self) -> BoundConstness {\n        self.skip_binder().constness\n    }\n}\n\n/// Encodes that `a` must be a subtype of `b`. existential predicates.\n   293→    ///\n   294→    /// A Rust trait object type consists (in addition to a lifetime bound)\n   295→    /// of a set of trait bounds, which are separated into any number\n   296→    /// of auto-trait bounds, and at most one non-auto-trait bound. The\n   297→    /// non-auto-trait bound is called the \"principal\" of the trait\n   298→    /// object.\n   299→    ///\n   300→    /// Only the principal can have methods or type parameters (because\n   301→    /// auto traits can have neither of them). This is important, because\n   302→    /// it means the auto traits can be treated as an unordered set (methods\n   303→    /// would force an order for the vtable, while relating traits with\n   304→    /// type parameters without knowing the order to relate them in is\n   305→    /// a rather non-trivial task).\n   306→    ///\n   307→    /// For example, in the trait object `dyn std::fmt::Debug + Sync`, the\n   308→    /// principal bound is `Some(std::fmt::Debug)`, while the auto-trait bounds\n   309→    /// are the set `{Sync}`.\n   310→    ///\n   311→    /// It is also possible to have a \"trivial\" trait object that\n   312→    /// consists only of auto traits, with no principal - for example,\n   313→    /// `dyn Send + Sync`. In that case, the set of auto-trait bounds\n   314→    /// is `{Send, Sync}`, while there is no principal. These trait objects\n   315→    /// have a \"trivial\" vtable consisting of just the size, alignment,\n   316→    /// and destructor.\n   317→    pub fn principal(&self) -> Option<ty::Binder<'tcx,       ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => Some(did),\n   348→            _ => None,\n   349→        })\n   350→    }\n   351→\n   352→    pub fn without_auto_traits(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = ty::PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx>> {\n   353→        self.iter().filter(|predicate| {\n   354→            !matches!(predicate.as_ref().skip_binder(), ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(_))\n   355→        })\n   356→    }\n   357→}\n   358→\n   359→pub type PolyTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, TraitRef<'tcx>>;\n   360→pub type PolyExistentialTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>;\n   361→pub type PolyExistentialProjection<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>;\n   362→\n   363→impl<'tcx> Clause<'tcx> {\n   364→    /// Performs a instantiation suitable for going from a\n   365→    /// poly-trait-ref to supertraits that must hold if that\n   366→    /// poly-trait-ref holds. This is slightly different from a normal\n   367→    /// instantiation in terms of what happens with bound regions. See\n   368→    /// lengthy comment below for details.\n   369→    pub fn instantiate_supertrait(\n   370→        self,\n   371→        tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n   372→        trait_ref: ty::PolyTraitRef<'tcx>,\n   373→    ) -> Clause<'tcx> {\n   374→        // The interaction between HRTB and supertraits is not entirely\n   375→        // obvious. Let me walk you (and myself) through an example.\n   376→        //\n   377→        // Let's start with an easy case. Consider two traits:\n   378→        //\n   379→        //     trait Foo<'a>: Bar<'a,'a> { }\n   380→        //     trait Bar<'b,'c> { }\n   381→        //\n   382→        // Now, if we have a trait reference `for<'x> T: Foo<'x>`, then\n   383→        // we can deduce that `for<'x> T: Bar<'x,'x>`. Basically, if we\n   384→        // knew that `Foo<'x>` (for any 'x) then we also know that\n   385→        // `Bar<'x,'x>` (for any 'x). This more-or-less falls out from\n   386→        // normal instantiation.\n   387→        //\n   388→        // In terms of why this is sound, the idea is that whenever there\n   389→        // is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>`, it must show that `T:Bar<'a,'a>`\n   390→        // holds. So if there is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>` that applies to\n   391→        // all `'a`, then we must know that `T:Bar<'a,'a>` holds for all\n   392→        // `'a`.\n   393→        //\n   394→        // Another example to be careful of is this:\n   395→        //\n   396→        //     trait Foo1<'a>: for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b> { }\n   397→        //     trait Bar1<'b,'c> { }\n   398→        //\n   399→        // Here, if we have `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`, then what do we know?\n   400→        // The answer is that we know `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`. The\n   401→        // reason is similar to the previous example: any impl of\n   402→        // `T:Foo1<'x>` must show that `for<'b> T: Bar1<'x, 'b>`. So\n   403→        // basically we would want to collapse the bound lifetimes from\n   404→        // the input (`trait_ref`) and the supertraits.\n   405→        //\n   406→        // To achieve this in practice is fairly straightforward. Let's\n   407→        // consider the more complicated scenario:\n   408→        //\n   409→        // - We start out with `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`. In this case, `'x`\n   410→        //   has a De Bruijn index of 1. We want to produce `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`,\n   411→        //   where both `'x` and `'b` would have a DB index of 1.\n   412→        //   The instantiation from the input trait-ref is therefore going to be\n   413→        //   `'a => 'x` (where `'x` has a DB index of 1).\n   414→        // - The supertrait-ref is `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, where `'a` is an\n   415→        //   early-bound parameter and `'b` is a late-bound parameter with a\n   416→        //   DB index of 1.\n   417→        // - If we replace `'a` with `'x` from the input, it too will have\n   418→        //   a DB index of 1, and thus we'll have `for<'x,'b> Bar1<'x,'b>`\n   419→        //   just as we wanted.\n   420→        //\n   421→        // There is only one catch. If we just apply the instantiation `'a\n   422→        // => 'x` to `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, the instantiation code will\n   423→        // adjust the DB index because we instantiating into a binder (it\n   424→        // tries to be so smart...) resulting in `for<'x> for<'b>\n   425→        // Bar1<'x,'b>` (we have no syntax for this, so use your\n   426→        // imagination). Basically the 'x will have DB index of 2 and 'b\n   427→        // will have DB index of 1. Not quite what we want. So we apply\n   428→        // the instantiation to the *contents* of the trait reference,\n   429→        // rather than the trait reference itself (put another way, the\n   430→        // instantiation code expects equal binding levels in the values\n   431→        // from the instantiation and the value being instantiated into, and\n   432→        // this trick achieves that).\n   433→\n   434→        // Working through the second example:\n   435→        // trait_ref: for<'x> T: Foo1<'^0.0>; args: [T, '^0.0]\n   436→        // predicate: for<'b> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0>; args: [Self, 'a, '^0.0]\n   437→        // We want to end up with:\n   438→        //     for<'x, 'b> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n   439→        // To do this:\n   440→        // 1) We must shift all bound vars in predicate by the length\n   441→        //    of trait ref's bound vars. So, we would end up with predicate like\n   442→        //    Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\n   443→        // 2) We can then apply the trait args to this, ending up with\n   444→        //    T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n   445→        // 3) Finally, to create the final bound vars, we concatenate the bound\n   446→        //    vars of the trait ref with those of the predicate:\n   447→        //    ['x, 'b]\n   448→        let bound_pred = self.kind();\n   449→        let pred_bound_vars = bound_pred.bound_vars();\n   450→        let trait_bound_vars = trait_ref.bound_vars();\n   451→        // 1) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0> -> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\n   452→        let shifted_pred =\n   453→            tcx.shift_bound_var_indices(trait_bound_vars.len(), bound_pred.skip_binder());\n   454→        // 2) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1> -> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n   455→        let new = EarlyBinder::bind(shifted_pred).instantiate(tcx, trait_ref.skip_binder().args);\n   456→        // 3) ['x] + ['b] -> ['x, 'b]\n   457→        let bound_vars =\n   458→            tcx.mk_bound_variable_kinds_from_iter(trait_bound_vars.iter().chain(pred_bound_vars));\n   459→\n   460→        // FIXME: Is it really perf sensitive to use reuse_or_mk_predicate here?\n   461→        tcx.reuse_or_mk_predicate(\n   462→            self.as_predicate(),\n   463→            ty::Binder::bind_with_vars(PredicateKind::Clause(new), bound_vars),\n   464→        )\n   465→        .expect_clause()\n   466→    }\n   467→}\n   468→\n   469→impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, PredicateKind<'tcx>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\n   470→    fn upcast_from(from: PredicateKind<'tcx>, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Self {\n   471→        ty::Binder::dummy(from).upcast(tcx)\n   472→    }\n   473→}\n   474→\n   475→impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, tcx.mk_predicate(from)\n   478→    }\n   479→}\n   480→\n   481→impl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, ClauseKind<'tcx>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\n   482→    fn upcast_from(from: ClauseKind<'tcx>, tcx: DebruijnIndex {\n        self.0.outer_exclusive_binder\n    }\n\n    /// Flips the polarity of a Predicate.\n    ///\n    /// Given `T: Trait` predicate it returns `T: !Trait` and given `T: !Trait` returns `T: Trait`.\n    pub fn flip_polarity(self, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Option<Predicate<'tcx>> {\n        let kind = self\n            .kind()\n            .map_bound(|kind| match kind {\n                PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::Trait(TraitPredicate {\n                    trait_ref,\n                    polarity,\n                })) => Some(PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::Trait(TraitPredicate {\n                    trait_ref,\n                    polarity: polarity.flip(),\n                }))),\n\n                _ => None,\n            })\n            .transpose()?;\n\n        Some(tcx.mk_predicate(kind))\n    }\n\n    /// Whether this projection can be soundly normalized.\n    ///\n    /// Wf predicates must not be normalized, as normalization\n    /// can remove required bounds which would cause us to\n    /// unsoundly accept some programs. See #91068.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn allow_normalization(self) -> bool {\n        match self.kind().skip_binder() {\n            PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::WellFormed(_)) | PredicateKind::AliasRelate(..) => {\n                false\n            }\n            PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::Trait(_))\n            | PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::HostEffect(..))\n            | PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::RegionOutlives(_))\n            | PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::TypeOutlives(_))\n            | PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::Projection(_))\n            | PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::ConstArgHasType(..))\n            | PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::UnstableFeature(_))\n            | PredicateKind::DynCompatible(_)\n            | PredicateKind::Subtype(_)\n            | PredicateKind::Coerce(_)\n            | PredicateKind::Clause(ClauseKind::ConstEvaluatable(_))\n            | PredicateKind::ConstEquate(_, _)\n            | PredicateKind::NormalizesTo(..)\n            | PredicateKind::Ambiguous => true,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> rustc_errors::IntoDiagArg for Predicate<'tcx> {\n    fn into_diag_arg(self, path: &mut Option<std::path::PathBuf>) -> rustc_errors::DiagArgValue {\n        ty::tls::with(|tcx| {\n            let pred = tcx.short_string(self, path);\n            rustc_errors::DiagArgValue::Str(std::borrow::Cow::Owned(pred))\n        })\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> rustc_errors::IntoDiagArg for Clause<'tcx> {\n    fn into_diag_arg(self, path: &mut Option<std::path::PathBuf>) -> rustc_errors::DiagArgValue {\n        ty::tls::with(|tcx| {\n            let clause = tcx.short_string(self, path);\n            rustc_errors::DiagArgValue::Str(std::borrow::Cow::Owned(clause))\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n/// A subset of predicates which can be assumed by the trait solver.       None\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn as_region_outlives_clause(\n        self,\n    ) -> Option<ty::Binder<'tcx, RegionOutlivesPredicate<'tcx>>> {\n        let clause = self.kind();\n        if rustc_type_ir::inherent::Clauses<TyCtxt<'tcx>> for ty::Clauses<'tcx> {}\n\n#[extension(pub trait ExistentialPredicateStableCmpExt<'tcx>)]\nimpl<'tcx> ExistentialPredicate<'tcx> {\n    /// Compares via an ordering that will not change if modules are reordered or other changes are\n    /// made to the tree. In particular, this ordering is preserved across incremental compilations.\n    fn stable_cmp(&self, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>, other: &Self) -> Ordering {\n        match (*self, *other) {\n            (ExistentialPredicate::Trait(_), ExistentialPredicate::Trait(_)) => Ordering::Equal,\n            (ExistentialPredicate::Projection(ref a), ExistentialPredicate::Projection(ref b)) => {\n                tcx.def_path_hash(a.def_id).cmp(&tcx.def_path_hash(b.def_id))\n            }\n            (ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(ref a), ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(ref b)) => {\n                tcx.def_path_hash(*a).cmp(&tcx.def_path_hash(*b))\n            }\n            (ExistentialPredicate::Trait(_), _) => Ordering::Less,\n            (ExistentialPredicate::Projection(_), ExistentialPredicate::Trait(_)) => {\n                Ordering::Greater\n            }\n            (ExistentialPredicate::Projection(_), _) => Ordering::Less,\n            (ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(_), _) => Ordering::Greater,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\npub type PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialPredicate<'tcx>>;\n\nimpl<'tcx> rustc_type_ir::inherent::BoundExistentialPredicates<TyCtxt<'tcx>>\n    for &'tcx ty::List<ty::PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx>>\n{\n    fn principal_def_id(self) -> Option<DefId> {\n        self.principal_def_id()\n    }\n\n    fn principal(self) -> Option<ty::PolyExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>> {\n        self.principal()\n    }\n\n    fn auto_traits(self) -> impl IntoIterator<Item = DefId> {\n        self.auto_traits()\n    }\n\n    fn projection_bounds(\n        self,\n    ) -> impl IntoIterator<Item = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>> {\n        self.projection_bounds()\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> ty::List<ty::PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx>> {\n    /// Returns the \"principal `DefId`\" of this set of existential predicates.\n    ///\n    /// A Rust trait object type consists (in addition to a lifetime bound)\n    /// of a set of trait bounds, which are separated into any number\n    /// of auto-trait bounds, and at most one non-auto-trait bound. The\n    /// non-auto-trait bound is called the \"principal\" of the trait\n    /// object.\n    ///\n    /// Only the principal can have methods or type parameters (because\n    /// auto traits can have neither of them). This is important, because\n    /// it means the auto traits can be treated as an unordered set (methods\n    /// would force an order for the vtable, while relating traits with\n    /// type parameters without knowing the order to relate them in is\n    /// a rather non-trivial task).\n    ///\n    /// For example, in the trait object `dyn std::fmt::Debug + Sync`, the\n    /// principal bound is `Some(std::fmt::Debug)`, while the auto-trait bounds\n    /// are the set `{Sync}`.\n    ///\n    /// It is also possible to have a \"trivial\" trait object that\n    /// consists only of auto traits, with no principal - for example,\n    /// `dyn Send + Sync`. In that case, the set of auto-trait bounds\n    /// is `{Send, Sync}`, while there is no principal. These trait objects\n    /// have a \"trivial\" vtable consisting of just the size, alignment,\n    /// and destructor.\n    pub fn principal(&self) -> Option<ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>> {\n        self[0]\n            .map_bound(|this| match this {\n                ExistentialPredicate::Trait(tr) => Some(tr),\n                _ => None,\n            })\n            .transpose()\n    }\n\n    pub fn principal_def_id(&self) -> Option<DefId> {\n        self.principal().map(|trait_ref| trait_ref.skip_binder().def_id)\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn projection_bounds(\n        &self,\n    ) -> impl Iterator<Item = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>> {\n        self.iter().filter_map(|predicate| {\n            predicate\n                .map_bound(|pred| match pred {\n                    ExistentialPredicate::Projection(projection) => Some(projection),\n                    _ => None,\n                })\n                .transpose()\n        })\n    }\n\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn auto_traits(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = DefId> {\n        self.iter().filter_map(|predicate| match predicate.skip_binder() {\n            ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(did) => Some(did),\n            _ => None,\n        })\n    }\n\n    pub fn without_auto_traits(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item = ty::PolyExistentialPredicate<'tcx>> {\n        self.iter().filter(|predicate| {\n            !matches!(predicate.as_ref().skip_binder(), ExistentialPredicate::AutoTrait(_))\n        })\n    }\n}\n\npub type PolyTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, TraitRef<'tcx>>;\npub type PolyExistentialTraitRef<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialTraitRef<'tcx>>;\npub type PolyExistentialProjection<'tcx> = ty::Binder<'tcx, ExistentialProjection<'tcx>>;\n\nimpl<'tcx> Clause<'tcx> {\n    /// Performs a instantiation suitable for going from a\n    /// poly-trait-ref to supertraits that must hold if that\n    /// poly-trait-ref holds. This is slightly different from a normal\n    /// instantiation in terms of what happens with bound regions. See\n    /// lengthy comment below for details.\n    pub fn instantiate_supertrait(\n        self,\n        tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\n        trait_ref: ty::PolyTraitRef<'tcx>,\n    ) -> Clause<'tcx> {\n        // The interaction between HRTB and supertraits is not entirely\n        // obvious. Let me walk you (and myself) through an example.\n        //\n        // Let's start with an easy case. Consider two traits:\n        //\n        //     trait Foo<'a>: Bar<'a,'a> { }\n        //     trait Bar<'b,'c> { }\n        //\n        // Now, if we have a trait reference `for<'x> T: Foo<'x>`, then\n        // we can deduce that `for<'x> T: Bar<'x,'x>`. Basically, if we\n        // knew that `Foo<'x>` (for any 'x) then we also know that\n        // `Bar<'x,'x>` (for any 'x). This more-or-less falls out from\n        // normal instantiation.\n        //\n        // In terms of why this is sound, the idea is that whenever there\n        // is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>`, it must show that `T:Bar<'a,'a>`\n        // holds. So if there is an impl of `T:Foo<'a>` that applies to\n        // all `'a`, then we must know that `T:Bar<'a,'a>` holds for all\n        // `'a`.\n        //\n        // Another example to be careful of is this:\n        //\n        //     trait Foo1<'a>: for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b> { }\n        //     trait Bar1<'b,'c> { }\n        //\n        // Here, if we have `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`, then what do we know?\n        // The answer is that we know `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`. The\n        // reason is similar to the previous example: any impl of\n        // `T:Foo1<'x>` must show that `for<'b> T: Bar1<'x, 'b>`. So\n        // basically we would want to collapse the bound lifetimes from\n        // the input (`trait_ref`) and the supertraits.\n        //\n        // To achieve this in practice is fairly straightforward. Let's\n        // consider the more complicated scenario:\n        //\n        // - We start out with `for<'x> T: Foo1<'x>`. In this case, `'x`\n        //   has a De Bruijn index of 1. We want to produce `for<'x,'b> T: Bar1<'x,'b>`,\n        //   where both `'x` and `'b` would have a DB index of 1.\n        //   The instantiation from the input trait-ref is therefore going to be\n        //   `'a => 'x` (where `'x` has a DB index of 1).\n        // - The supertrait-ref is `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, where `'a` is an\n        //   early-bound parameter and `'b` is a late-bound parameter with a\n        //   DB index of 1.\n        // - If we replace `'a` with `'x` from the input, it too will have\n        //   a DB index of 1, and thus we'll have `for<'x,'b> Bar1<'x,'b>`\n        //   just as we wanted.\n        //\n        // There is only one catch. If we just apply the instantiation `'a\n        // => 'x` to `for<'b> Bar1<'a,'b>`, the instantiation code will\n        // adjust the DB index because we instantiating into a binder (it\n        // tries to be so smart...) resulting in `for<'x> for<'b>\n        // Bar1<'x,'b>` (we have no syntax for this, so use your\n        // imagination). Basically the 'x will have DB index of 2 and 'b\n        // will have DB index of 1. Not quite what we want. So we apply\n        // the instantiation to the *contents* of the trait reference,\n        // rather than the trait reference itself (put another way, the\n        // instantiation code expects equal binding levels in the values\n        // from the instantiation and the value being instantiated into, and\n        // this trick achieves that).\n\n        // Working through the second example:\n        // trait_ref: for<'x> T: Foo1<'^0.0>; args: [T, '^0.0]\n        // predicate: for<'b> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0>; args: [Self, 'a, '^0.0]\n        // We want to end up with:\n        //     for<'x, 'b> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n        // To do this:\n        // 1) We must shift all bound vars in predicate by the length\n        //    of trait ref's bound vars. So, we would end up with predicate like\n        //    Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\n        // 2) We can then apply the trait args to this, ending up with\n        //    T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n        // 3) Finally, to create the final bound vars, we concatenate the bound\n        //    vars of the trait ref with those of the predicate:\n        //    ['x, 'b]\n        let bound_pred = self.kind();\n        let pred_bound_vars = bound_pred.bound_vars();\n        let trait_bound_vars = trait_ref.bound_vars();\n        // 1) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.0> -> Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1>\n        let shifted_pred =\n            tcx.shift_bound_var_indices(trait_bound_vars.len(), bound_pred.skip_binder());\n        // 2) Self: Bar1<'a, '^0.1> -> T: Bar1<'^0.0, '^0.1>\n        let new = EarlyBinder::bind(shifted_pred).instantiate(tcx, trait_ref.skip_binder().args);\n        // 3) ['x] + ['b] -> ['x, 'b]\n        let bound_vars =\n            tcx.mk_bound_variable_kinds_from_iter(trait_bound_vars.iter().chain(pred_bound_vars));\n\n        // FIXME: Is it really perf sensitive to use reuse_or_mk_predicate here?\n        tcx.reuse_or_mk_predicate(\n            self.as_predicate(),\n            ty::Binder::bind_with_vars(PredicateKind::Clause(new), bound_vars),\n        )\n        .expect_clause()\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, PredicateKind<'tcx>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\n    fn upcast_from(from: PredicateKind<'tcx>, tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>) -> Self {\n        ty::Binder::dummy(from).upcast(tcx)\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'tcx> UpcastFrom<TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty::Binder<'tcx, PredicateKind<'tcx>>> for Predicate<'tcx> {\n    fn upcast_from(from: ty::Binder<'tcx, SubtypePredicate → SubtypeRelation Refactoring - Quick Start\n\n## What This Is\n\nA complete refactoring of the Rust compiler to rename `SubtypePredicate` to `SubtypeRelation` with clearer field names (`a` → `sub_ty`, `b` → `super_ty`).\n\n## The Problem\n\n**Before**: Field names `a` and `b` are opaque\n```rust\npub struct SubtypePredicate<I: Interner> {\n    pub a_is_expected: bool,\n
